style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,727,899</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+33.7%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1970</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">3,815,422</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+39.9%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1980</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">5,387,680</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+41.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1990</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">6,228,239</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+15.6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1995</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">6,737,324</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+8.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">6,908,975</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+2.5%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2005</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">7,110,214</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+2.9%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">2010</th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">7,643,194</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+7.5%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2015<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></th>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">8,112,505</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+6.1%</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The state of Veracruz, especially its port, has been a crossroads for various cultures since the very early colonial period. The port of Veracruz has brought cargo, sailors, seamen, and slaves from various parts of the world, especially from the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and Europe. The state has indigenous cultural influences mixed with those from Europe, Africa and the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" class="extiw" title="wikt:Afro-Caribbean">Afro-Caribbean</a>. These can be best seen in the music, the culinary traditions and in the people themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-khursh_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khursh-11">[11]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The number of ethnic communities in the state has been calculated at 2,062. The most numerous include the <a href="/wiki/Nahua_peoples" title="Nahua peoples">Nahuas</a>, Totonacs, Huastecs, Popolucs, <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_peoples" title="Zapotec peoples">Zapotecas</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinanteca_(people)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chinanteca (people) (page does not exist)">Chinantecas</a>, Otomis, Mazatecas, Tepehuas, Mixtecas, Zoques, <a href="/wiki/Mixe" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixe">Mixes</a>, Mayas and <a href="/wiki/Tzotzil_people" title="Tzotzil people">Tzotzils</a>, all indigenous groups. The largest are Nahuas, who make up over half of the indigenous population. Most native communities can be found in 68 municipalities especially in <a href="/wiki/Tehuipango" title="Tehuipango">Tehuipango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mixtla_de_Altamirano" title="Mixtla de Altamirano">Mixtla de Altamirano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astacinga" title="Astacinga">Astacinga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soledad_Atzompa" title="Soledad Atzompa">Soledad Atzompa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlahuilco" title="Atlahuilco">Atlahuilco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tequila,_Veracruz" title="Tequila, Veracruz">Tequila</a>, Tlaquilpan, Los Reyes, Magdalena, San Andres Tenejapan, Tantoyuca, Zongolica, Chicontepec, Papantla, Ixhuatl\xc3\xa1n de Madero, Soteapan, Playa Vicente, Mecayapan y Coyutla, Benito Ju\xc3\xa1rez, Coxquihi, Espinal, Filomeno Mata, Ixcatepec, Mecatl\xc3\xa1n and Zozocolco de Hidalgo. In 1998, about 10% of the population spoke an indigenous language; however, this does not take into account all indigenous peoples. The census of 2005 counted 605,135 as speaking an indigenous language.<sup id="cite_ref-perfilsoc_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perfilsoc-48">[48]</a></sup></p>\n<p>There are also small immigrant communities of Spaniards, Italians, Basque and <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup> African slaves were imported to Mexico through the Veracruz port. At one point, they outnumbered Europeans and a significant number ran away from haciendas and plantations to form their own communities, sometimes allied with indigenous groups. One such rebellion was led by Yanga, who successfully negotiated a free African community with Spanish authorities in 1609. Like other groups, many of African descent would intermarry with other groups, with the category of \xe2\x80\x9cmulatto\xe2\x80\x9d existing in the old colonial caste system for those with African blood. Today, the vast majority of <a href="/wiki/Afro_Mexican" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro Mexican">Afro Mexicans</a> in Veracruz and other parts of the country are spread out and intermixed with the rest of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-africanroots_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africanroots-49">[49]</a></sup></p>\n<p>With a population of 7,110,214 (2005), Veracruz is the third most populous entity in the country, after the Federal District of Mexico City and the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a>. Population growth has slowed in the state in the last decades, due to lower birthrates and the exodus of migrants, mostly men. Women outnumber men. One reason for the decline in birthrates is the elevation of education levels, especially among women. Another is urbanization, with about one-third of the state\xe2\x80\x99s population living in urban centers, especially Veracruz, Xalapa, Coatzacoalcos, Minatitl\xc3\xa1n and Papantla. Most (90%) of the state\xe2\x80\x99s communities, outside of municipal seats have fewer than 500 people and contain only 21% of the total population. The migration of men outside the state has put more women into the state\'s workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-perfilsoc_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perfilsoc-48">[48]</a></sup> Approximately 75% of the population is under 45 years of age and 30% under the age of 15.<sup id="cite_ref-habitantes_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-habitantes-50">[50]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:178px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leuchtturm_Veracruz_fcm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Leuchtturm_Veracruz_fcm.jpg/176px-Leuchtturm_Veracruz_fcm.jpg" width="176" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Leuchtturm_Veracruz_fcm.jpg/264px-Leuchtturm_Veracruz_fcm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Leuchtturm_Veracruz_fcm.jpg/352px-Leuchtturm_Veracruz_fcm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leuchtturm_Veracruz_fcm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nVeracruz lighthouse</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Life expectancy is just under the norm for the rest of the country. The overwhelming majority of people in the state are Catholic, however, there is a significant Protestant minority and a number who profess the Jewish faith.<sup id="cite_ref-perfilsoc_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perfilsoc-48">[48]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Tourism mostly centers on the <a href="/wiki/Port_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Port city">port city</a> of Veracruz but there are other destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup> There are over 1,000 hotels in the state, over half of which are small, family-owned enterprises. Almost all of the four and five-star establishments are in metropolitan area of Veracruz. Many of the state major historical and cultural monuments are located in the port of Veracruz. Some of these include the Aquarium, the Museum of the City (Museo de la Ciudad), The Agust\xc3\xadn Lara Museum, the Santiago Fortress (Baluarte de Santiago) the "Las Atarazanas" Museum and the San Juan de Ul\xc3\xbaa Fort.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>To the north of the port city is the Sierra or Totonacalpan area of the state, home to the Totonac people. This is home to the important pre-Hispanic city of <a href="/wiki/El_Taj%C3%ADn" title="El Taj\xc3\xadn">El Taj\xc3\xadn</a> and the present-day city of <a href="/wiki/Papantla" title="Papantla">Papantla</a>. The modern city is best known as the home of the Totonac version of the \xe2\x80\x9c<a href="/wiki/Danza_de_los_Voladores_de_Papantla" class="mw-redirect" title="Danza de los Voladores de Papantla">danza de voladores</a>\xe2\x80\x9d; there, the dancers spin from 80&#160;ft (24.4&#160;m) high poles. The area is also the native habitat of the vanilla bean.<sup id="cite_ref-khursh_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khursh-11">[11]</a></sup></p>\n<p>To the south of the port is on the coast, is Catemaco. This is in a tropical area. The area\xe2\x80\x99s two main features are <a href="/wiki/Lake_Catemaco" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Catemaco">Lake Catemaco</a>, which is located in the crater of an extinct volcano and Isla Tanaxpillo just off the coast. This island is also called the island of the monkeys or baboons due to a group of feral monkeys that escaped and found refuge here.<sup id="cite_ref-khursh_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khursh-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Inland is the coffee-growing region in and around the cities of Coatepec and Xalapa. Orizaba is best known for the volcano nearby but also has a large waterfall called El Elefante and a Ca\xc3\xb1on (Canyon) de R\xc3\xado Blanco.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Archeological_sites">Archeological sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Archeological sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The state contains numerous remains of pre-Hispanic <a href="/wiki/Olmec" title="Olmec">Olmec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Totonac" class="mw-redirect" title="Totonac">Totonac</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Huastec_civilization" title="Huastec civilization">Huastec</a> cities. El Taj\xc3\xadn, a ruined city that reached its apex between the 9th and 13th centuries ad, was designated a UNESCO World Heritage site in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-brittanica_14-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brittanica-14">[14]</a></sup></p>\n<p>El Zapotal is an archeological site which was discovered in 1971 in a region known at Mixtequlla (between the Blanco and Papaloapan Rivers). This site is noted for its clay figurines with smiling faces, part of an extremely large offering in honor of the god of death <a href="/wiki/Mictlantecuhtli" title="Mictlantecuhtli">Mictlantecuhtli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Cempoala is an archeological site located on the coast between the modern settlements of La Antigua and Ciudad Cardel. It was occupied when Hern\xc3\xa1n Cort\xc3\xa9s arrived, and he managed to form an alliance with the Totonacs here against the Aztecs. In the center of the site, there is a large plaza surrounded by temples and the palace of the Totonac chief. The site also has a small museum.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Taj%C3%ADn,_Nischenpyramide.fcm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/El_Taj%C3%ADn%2C_Nischenpyramide.fcm.jpg/230px-El_Taj%C3%ADn%2C_Nischenpyramide.fcm.jpg" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/El_Taj%C3%ADn%2C_Nischenpyramide.fcm.jpg/345px-El_Taj%C3%ADn%2C_Nischenpyramide.fcm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/El_Taj%C3%ADn%2C_Nischenpyramide.fcm.jpg/460px-El_Taj%C3%ADn%2C_Nischenpyramide.fcm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Taj%C3%ADn,_Nischenpyramide.fcm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nEl Taj\xc3\xadn, Niche pyramid</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Quiahuiztl\xc3\xa1n is on the coast on a small mountain named Bernal. It is cut into the mountain as a series of terraces. It is located very close to where Cort\xc3\xa9s founded the initial Spanish settlement of Villa Rica de la Vera-Cruz.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Castillo de Teayo (Teayo Castle) is really a pyramid, whose original name was Zapotitl\xc3\xa1n. It is located on the border between Huasctec and Totonac lands. It was abandoned in the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The largest and most important site is <a href="/wiki/El_Taj%C3%ADn" title="El Taj\xc3\xadn">El Taj\xc3\xadn</a>, located near the city of Papantla. The name is from the Totonac language and means \xe2\x80\x9cthunder,\xe2\x80\x9d but no one knows what the true name of this city was. It is also unknown if the Totonac built it, but since they have dominated the region for centuries, they lay claim to it.The city developed from the end of the Classic period and the beginning of the Post Classic period, between 800 and 1150 C.E. It is divided into five zones, the Plaza del Arroyo Group, the Central Zone, the Gran Xicalcoliuhqui, Taj\xc3\xadn Chico and the Column Complex. Its signature building is the Pyramid of the Niches, named after the 365 niches built into the levels of the structure. The site has a large number of Mesoamerican ball game courts, one with details reliefs showing the beheading of a ballplayer and his role in the afterlife.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Tres Zapotes site is located the community of the same name. Covering 1.5 hectares, the main building has a square base, which is surrounded by gardens and trees. The most important find from his is Stele \xe2\x80\x9cC\xe2\x80\x9d which is on display at the <a href="/wiki/Museo_Nacional_de_Antropolog%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Museo Nacional de Antropolog\xc3\xada">Museo Nacional de Antropolog\xc3\xada</a> in Mexico City.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>El Pital is a site in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADnez_de_la_Torre,_Veracruz" class="mw-redirect" title="Mart\xc3\xadnez de la Torre, Veracruz">Mart\xc3\xadnez de la Torre</a>. It consists of a mound with a pyramid base and stairs on the east side.The site\xe2\x80\x99s culture is considered to be a link between the coastal and highland cultures of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Los Idolos is a site in the municipal city of <a href="/wiki/Misantla" title="Misantla">Misantla</a>, and was an important ceremonial site for the Totonacapan region. It consists of four rectangular patios linked by platforms and flat-topped mounds. Many of the structures are decorated with smooth river stone, thought to have come from the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Misantla_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Misantla River (page does not exist)">Misantla River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Centro Ceremonial Cuajilote is located on the <a href="/wiki/Bobos_River_(Mexico)" title="Bobos River (Mexico)">Bobos River</a>. It consists of a large plaza 400 meters long lined with structures. In the center of the plaza there are three shrines, one of which contains phallic figures.<sup id="cite_ref-atractcul_35-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atractcul-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Veracruz became a state in 1824. Its government is headed by a governor, who is elected to a single term of six years. Members of the <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> legislature, the State Congress, are elected to three-year terms. The state is divided into 212 local governmental units called <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Mexico" title="Municipalities of Mexico">municipios (municipalities)</a>, each of which is headquartered in a prominent city, town, or village.<sup id="cite_ref-brittanica_14-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brittanica-14">[14]</a></sup> The newest of these are the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/San_Rafael,_Veracruz" title="San Rafael, Veracruz">San Rafael</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Sochiapan" title="Santiago Sochiapan">Santiago Sochiapan</a> which were created in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-gobierno_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gobierno-51">[51]</a></sup> These municipalities are grouped into regions called Huasteca Alta (with ten municipalities), Huasteca Baja (with 23 municipalities), Totonac (with 15 municipalities), Nautla (with 11 municipalities), Capital (with 33 municipalities), Sotavento (with 12 municipalities), De las Monta\xc3\xb1as (with 57 municipalities), Papaloapan (with 22 municipalities), De los Tuxtlas (with four municipalities) and Olmeca (with 25 municipalities) .<sup id="cite_ref-regionalizacion_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regionalizacion-52">[52]</a></sup></p>\n<p><b>Freedom of the Press violations</b><br />\nAccording to many journalists\' organizations, Veracruz is one of the most dangerous places for journalists especially after governor <a href="/wiki/Javier_Duarte_de_Ochoa" title="Javier Duarte de Ochoa">Javier Duarte de Ochoa</a> came to power in December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The road system in the state contains 16,039&#160;km (9,966.2&#160;mi), representing 5.1% of the roads nationwide. For each 100&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (38.6&#160;sq&#160;mi) of territory, there are 22&#160;km (13.7&#160;mi) of roads. 3,144.5&#160;km (1,953.9&#160;mi) are part of the federal highway system. State roads comprise 2,176&#160;km (1,352.1&#160;mi) with the rest maintained by local authorities. There are over 3,000&#160;km (1,864.1&#160;mi) of rural roads, but only 71.5&#160;km (44.4&#160;mi) are paved.<sup id="cite_ref-infraes_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infraes-44">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The state contains 1,675.3&#160;km (1,041.0&#160;mi) of railway. Most of this is conceded by the federal government to private companies, with strategic stretches maintained directly by the government. Some of the private companies include <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Southern_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Kansas City Southern de M\xc3\xa9xico">Kansas City Southern de M\xc3\xa9xico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferrosur" title="Ferrosur">Ferrosur</a>. These lines are used almost exclusively for the transportation of freight, which in 1999 added up to 37 million tons. Three rail lines serve the port of Veracruz exclusively. One is dedicated to the port of Coatzacalcos.<sup id="cite_ref-infraes_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infraes-44">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The ports of Veracruz are Tuxpan, Veracruz, Coatzacoalcos, Pajaritos, Minatitl\xc3\xa1n-Nanchital, Tecolutla, <a href="/wiki/Nautla" class="mw-redirect" title="Nautla">Nautla</a>, Alvarado and Tlacotalpan. The first three are the ports for heavy cargo ships, with Veracruz the most important of the three. The others are small ports for small ships, fishing boats and tourism. All ports are operated privately with the exception of Pajaritos, which is operated by <a href="/wiki/PEMEX" class="mw-redirect" title="PEMEX">PEMEX</a>. Port traffic in Veracruz account for 10% of all commercial traffic in the country, 23.4% of the port traffic of Mexico and 21% of all port traffic in the Gulf of Mexico and Caribbean. Goods imported through the state reach 16 out of Mexico\xe2\x80\x99s 31 states plus Mexico City. The port of Veracruz alone handles over 12 million tons of freight per year. Coatzacoalcos is important for its handling of petroleum products.<sup id="cite_ref-infraes_44-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infraes-44">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The state contains three major airports. \xe2\x80\x9cEl Taj\xc3\xadn\xe2\x80\x9d in Tihuatl\xc3\xa1n serving Poza Rica and \xe2\x80\x9cCanticas\xe2\x80\x9d in Minatitl\xc3\xa1n provide national service. \xe2\x80\x9cHeriberto Jara Corona\xe2\x80\x9d in the city of Veracruz provides national and international service. There are also 31 smaller regional airfields in municipalities such as Acayuc\xc3\xa1n, <a href="/wiki/Cazones_de_Herrera" title="Cazones de Herrera">Cazones de Herrera</a>, C\xc3\xb3rdoba, <a href="/wiki/Cuitl%C3%A1huac,_Veracruz" title="Cuitl\xc3\xa1huac, Veracruz">Cuitlahuac</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ju%C3%A1n_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Clara&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ju\xc3\xa1n Rodr\xc3\xadguez Clara (page does not exist)">Ju\xc3\xa1n Rodr\xc3\xadguez Clara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ozuluama" title="Ozuluama">Ozuluama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plat%C3%B3n_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Plat\xc3\xb3n S\xc3\xa1nchez">Plat\xc3\xb3n S\xc3\xa1nchez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Playa_Vicente" title="Playa Vicente">Playa Vicente</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soconusco" title="Soconusco">Soconusco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamal%C3%ADn" title="Tamal\xc3\xadn">Tamal\xc3\xadn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamiahua" title="Tamiahua">Tamiahua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tecolutla" title="Tecolutla">Tecolutla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temapache" title="Temapache">Temapache</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tempoal_de_S%C3%A1nchez,_Veracruz" title="Tempoal de S\xc3\xa1nchez, Veracruz">Tempoal</a> and Tierra Blanca.<sup id="cite_ref-infraes_44-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infraes-44">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<p>There are 59 local newspapers and 40 magazines published in the state. These include the Diario de Xalapa, El Dictamen, El Sol del Centro and la Opini\xc3\xb3n de Minatitl\xc3\xa1n. There are 202 radio stations (57 AM, 35 FM). Most are commercial or private but some are operated by non-profits and governmental agencies. There are 22 television stations; two channels are local, and the rest are repeaters from national broadcasters. Five companies provide cable and satellite television. <a href="/wiki/Telmex" title="Telmex">Telmex</a> controls over 75% of the telephone service in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-infraes_44-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infraes-44">[44]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_communities">Major communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Veracruz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Major communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Acayucan" title="Acayucan">Acayucan</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alvarado,_Veracruz" title="Alvarado, Veracruz">Alvarado</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Boca_del_R%C3%ADo,_Veracruz" title="Boca del R\xc3\xado, Veracruz">Boca del R\xc3\xado</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Camar%C3%B3n_de_Tejeda" title="Camar\xc3\xb3n de Tejeda">Camar\xc3\xb3n de Tejeda</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Catemaco" title="Catemaco">Catemaco</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Coatepec,_Veracruz" title="Coatepec, Veracruz">Coatepec</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Coatzacoalcos" title="Coatzacoalcos">Coatzacoalcos</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Veracruz" title="C\xc3\xb3rdoba, Veracruz">C\xc3\xb3rdoba</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/El_J%C3%ADcaro,_Veracruz" title="El J\xc3\xadcaro, Veracruz">El J\xc3\xadcaro, Veracruz</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADnez_de_la_Torre" title="Mart\xc3\xadnez de la Torre">Mart\xc3\xadnez de la Torre</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Minatitl%C3%A1n,_Veracruz" title="Minatitl\xc3\xa1n, Veracruz">Minatitl\xc3\xa1n</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Orizaba" title="Orizaba">Orizaba</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Papantla" title="Papantla">Papantla (Papantla de Olarte)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Poza_Rica" title="Poza Rica">Poza Rica</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Santiago_Tuxtla" title="Santiago Tuxtla">Santiago Tuxtla</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Andr%C3%A9s_Tuxtla" title="San Andr\xc3\xa9s Tuxtla">San Andr\xc3\xa9s Tuxtla</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tuxpan" title="Tuxpan">Tuxpan</a> (T\xc3\xbaxpam/T\xc3\xbaxpam de Rodr\xc3\xadguez Cano)]]</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Veracruz_(city)" title="Veracruz (city)">Veracruz</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Xalapa" title="Xalapa">Xalapa (Xalapa-Enr\xc3\xadquez)</a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Portal:Mexico">Mexico portal</a></span></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://biblio.juridicas.unam.mx/libros/6/2920/11.pdf">"Las Diputaciones Provinciales"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span> (in Spanish). p.&#160;15.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AVeracruz&amp;rft.atitle=Las+Diputaciones+Provinciales&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.pages=15&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbiblio.juridicas.unam.mx%2Flibros%2F6%2F2920%2F11.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nettie_Lee_Benson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nettie Lee Benson (page does not exist)">Nettie Lee
